/></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Utuado</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;u\xcb\x88twa\xc3\xb0o&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Utuado_barrio-pueblo" title="Utuado barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located in the central mountainous region of the island known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a></i>. It is located north of <a href="/wiki/Adjuntas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Adjuntas, Puerto Rico">Adjuntas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>; south of <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Lares,_Puerto_Rico" title="Lares, Puerto Rico">Lares</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ciales, Puerto Rico">Ciales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a>. It is the third-largest municipality in land area in Puerto Rico (after <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>). According to the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_census" title="2020 United States census">2020 US Census</a>, the municipality has a population of 28,287 spread over 24 <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utuado_barrio-pueblo" title="Utuado barrio-pueblo">Utuado pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city).\n</p><p>Utuado is the main municipality of the Utuado <a href="/wiki/Micropolitan_statistical_area" title="Micropolitan statistical area">micropolitan statistical area</a> and is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_metropolitan_area#Combined_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan-Caguas-Fajardo Combined Statistical Area</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology_and_nicknames">Etymology and nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The name Utuado derives from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> word <i>otoao</i>, meaning roughly <i>between mountains</i> (i.e., a valley). The letters "o" and "u" are often variable in Ta\xc3\xadno. The "d" originated as a <a href="/wiki/Hypercorrection" title="Hypercorrection">hypercorrection</a>: colloquial Spanish often reduces /a\xc3\xb0o/ to /ao/, so an un-etymological "d" was added to the Ta\xc3\xadno name.\n</p><p>The municipality is known as <i>Ciudad del Viv\xc3\xad</i> (Viv\xc3\xad City), derived from the <a href="/wiki/Viv%C3%AD_River" title="Viv\xc3\xad River">Viv\xc3\xad River</a> which runs through Utuado: one river branch comes from <a href="/wiki/Adjuntas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Adjuntas, Puerto Rico">Adjuntas</a> and the other from <a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a>. These two rivers then meet near the <a href="/wiki/Fernando_L._Ribas_Dominicci" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernando L. Ribas Dominicci">Fernando L. Ribas Dominicci</a> Avenue and continue the journey to <a href="/wiki/Lago_Dos_Bocas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lago Dos Bocas">Lago Dos Bocas</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The town of Utuado was founded October 12, 1739, by <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irishman</a> Sebastian de Morfi (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Sebastian_Murphy_(settler)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sebastian Murphy (settler) (page does not exist)">Sebastian Murphy</a>), on behalf of 60 families from <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was the first town established in the interior, mountainous region of the island known as <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> and the 11th oldest established municipality in Puerto Rico, following <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Germ\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coamo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Coamo, Puerto Rico">Coamo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aguada,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguada, Puerto Rico">Aguada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza,_Puerto_Rico" title="Lo\xc3\xadza, Puerto Rico">Loiza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>, <a href="/wiki/A%C3%B1asco" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xb1asco">A\xc3\xb1asco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guayama, Puerto Rico">Guayama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manat%C3%AD,_Puerto_Rico" title="Manat\xc3\xad, Puerto Rico">Manat\xc3\xad</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Columbus\'s_arrival"><span id="Columbus.27s_arrival"></span>Columbus\'s arrival</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Columbus&#039;s arrival"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>At the time of the Spanish initial occupation of the island on November 19, 1493, by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, Puerto Rico was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a>. The Ta\xc3\xadnos were a culturally developed society with a universal <a href="/wiki/Natural_language" title="Natural language">language</a>, a developed agricultural system, and a social organization based on <i>caciques</i> or <a href="/wiki/Tribal_chief" title="Tribal chief">chieftains</a>. The Utuado area was ruled over by cacique Guarionex. In <a href="/wiki/Caguana,_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguana, Utuado, Puerto Rico">Caguana</a>, the Ta\xc3\xadnos built a series of courts or <i>bateyes</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Caguana_Ceremonial_Ball_Courts_Site" title="Caguana Ceremonial Ball Courts Site">Caguana Ceremonial Ball Courts Site</a></i>, the most extensive example of Taino engineering in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nhlsum_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhlsum-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The site is designated a US National Historic Landmark.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLnom_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLnom-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_history:_XVI\xe2\x80\x93XVIII_centuries"><span id="Early_history:_XVI.E2.80.93XVIII_centuries"></span>Early history: XVI\xe2\x80\x93XVIII centuries</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early history: XVI\xe2\x80\x93XVIII centuries"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>From 1510 through 1513, the island witnessed a Ta\xc3\xadno rebellion as a result of harsh and inhumane treatment by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish settlers</a>. During the process of pacification many <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> settled in the area now occupied by the municipality of Utuado and set up farms (<i>haciendas</i>), initially on behalf of the Spanish government (<i>Hacienda Real Dos</i>), to provide food for the Indian slaves working the <a href="/wiki/Gold_mining" title="Gold mining">gold mines</a> and the Spanish colonists in the area. One of the first settlers in the Otoao region in 1512 was <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Sede%C3%B1o" title="Antonio Sede\xc3\xb1o">Antonio Sede\xc3\xb1o</a>, the island\'s <a href="/wiki/Bookkeeping" title="Bookkeeping">bookkeeper</a>. His farm\'s main crop was <i><a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">yuca</a></i>. His farm was sold in 1519 to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Blas_de_Villasante&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Blas de Villasante (page does not exist)">Blas de Villasante</a>, the island\'s treasurer, for 525 gold <i>pesos</i>.\n</p><p>Areas in the Utuado region that were exploited for gold include <a href="/wiki/Salto_Arriba" title="Salto Arriba">Salto Arriba</a> barrio, initially, then later in the 1530s <a href="/wiki/Caguana,_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguana, Utuado, Puerto Rico">Caguana</a> barrio and <a href="/wiki/Don_Alonso" title="Don Alonso">Don Alonso</a> barrio. In the 1530s, landowners in the Don Alonso area petitioned the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spanish_monarchs" title="List of Spanish monarchs">Spanish Crown</a> allow for the establishment of a town in the area but it was never granted.\n</p><p>Once the gold mining era ended toward the end of the 16th century, very little is known about the Utuado region until the early 18th century. According to the Puerto Rican historian <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pic%C3%B3" title="Fernando Pic\xc3\xb3">Fernando Pic\xc3\xb3</a>, the few documents that exist indicate the area was mostly unpopulated and densely <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_moist_forests" title="Puerto Rican moist forests">forested</a>. On the other hand, he states that Utuado is the municipality with the most caves, that most likely served as dwellings for Indians or runaway slaves.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg/220px-UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg/330px-UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg/440px-UtuadoStreetScene1899small.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="452" /></a><figcaption>"Utuado Street Scene" from <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Weekly" title="Harper&#39;s Weekly">Harper\'s Weekly</a></i> May 13, 1899</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The agreement to establish the town of Utuado by the 60 families of Arecibo states they purchased the <i><b>Hato de Otoao</b></i> for 569 <a href="/wiki/Peso" title="Peso">pesos</a> and 5 reales from owners Manuel Natal and Felipa Rom\xc3\xa1n. It also states their desire to choose where on the land the town center would be located, which indicates the area was not populated yet.\n</p><p>During his visit to the island in 1771, <a href="/wiki/Fray_I%C3%B1igo_Abbad_y_Lasierra" class="mw-redirect" title="Fray I\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra">Fray I\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra</a> states the principal economic activity in the Utuado region was <a href="/wiki/Cattle_raising" class="mw-redirect" title="Cattle raising">cattle raising</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mule" title="Mule">mules</a>. He mentions a small amount of agricultural activity existed but the population only produced enough tobacco and coffee for their own consumption.\n</p><p>During the late 18th and early 19th centuries, Utuado\'s population continued to grow as coffee gained in importance and growers saw the need for high altitudes and mountainous terrain to produce the best <a href="/wiki/Coffee_bean" title="Coffee bean">coffee beans</a>. People not only <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migrated</a> from the Puerto Rican coastal towns but also from Ireland (founder Sebastian de Morfi was Irish), the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Majorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Majorca">Majorca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>, all seeking the riches that coffee had to offer.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Golden_era_of_coffee_\xe2\x80\x93_&quot;black_gold&quot;"><span id="Golden_era_of_coffee_.E2.80.93_.22black_gold.22"></span>Golden era of coffee \xe2\x80\x93 "black gold"</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Golden era of coffee \xe2\x80\x93 &quot;black gold&quot;"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg/250px-Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg/375px-Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg/500px-Utuado1896GoldenEra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="770" /></a><figcaption>Utuado in 1896 during the coffee golden era</figcaption></figure>\n<p>During the late 19th century Utuado experienced an explosive economic growth centered around the cultivation of coffee, also known at the time as <i>oro negro</i> or "black gold". By the 1890s Utuado was the largest producer of coffee in Puerto Rico and the second municipality (after <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>) with the largest population. It produced a rich social life for many of its citizens and a casino and theatre were established in the town. The progress of the town was so evident that the regent Queen of Spain, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Christina_of_Austria" title="Maria Christina of Austria">Mar\xc3\xada Cristina</a>, honored the town with the title of <i>Ciudad</i> (City) on August 20, 1894.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1896 or 1897 Utuado was the first city in Puerto Rico with a <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">public electric lighting</a> system powered by a <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_turbine" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydraulic turbine">hydraulic turbine</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Power plant">power plant</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in that same year mayor Juan Casellas planned a train system to connect Utuado with Arecibo. By 1899 this golden era ended due to two events: the United States <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">occupation of the island in 1898</a>, which made sugar the new crop of importance instead of coffee (Utuado\'s mountainous landscape was not ideal for growing <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, making it impossible for it to compete in the sugar industry), and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_San_Ciriaco" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane San Ciriaco">Hurricane San Ciriaco</a> in 1899, which destroyed the coffee <i>haciendas</i>.\n</p><p>Utuado was the first municipality to elect officials after Spain ceded Puerto Rico to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Massacre">Massacre</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Massacre"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg/200px-El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg/300px-El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg/400px-El_Imparcial_Utuado.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="958" /></a><figcaption>El Imparcial headline: "Aviation (US) bombs Utuado"</figcaption></figure>\n<p>One of the most tragic moments in Utuado\'s history occurred on October 30, 1950, during the <a href="/wiki/Utuado_uprising" title="Utuado uprising">Utuado uprising</a> against United States rule, which culminated in what is known as the <b>Utuado Massacre</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-HU_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HU-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In Utuado, a group of 32 nationalists, led by nationalist leaders Heriberto Castro and Dami\xc3\xa1n Torres, fought against the local police during the independence revolts which occurred in various cities and towns of the island. The group was reduced to 12 men and retreated to Dami\xc3\xa1n Torres\' house. Torres\' residence was attacked by 50-caliber machine-gun fire from ten American <a href="/wiki/P-47_Thunderbolt" class="mw-redirect" title="P-47 Thunderbolt">P-47 Thunderbolt</a> planes.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_(United_States)" title="National Guard (United States)">National Guard</a> arrived later that day and ordered the nine men who survived the attack to surrender. Once the nationalists surrendered, they were forced to march down Dr. Cueto Street to the main town square where their shoes, belts and personal belongings were removed. The group was then taken behind the police station where they were gunned down. Five of the nationalists died in the act, these were nationalist leader Heriberto Castro, Julio Col\xc3\xb3n Feliciano, Agust\xc3\xadn Qui\xc3\xb1ones Mercado, Antonio Ramos and Antonio Gonz\xc3\xa1lez. Gonz\xc3\xa1lez, who was 17&#160;years old, pleaded for water and instead was bayoneted to death.<sup id="cite_ref-HU_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HU-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hurricane_Maria">Hurricane Maria</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Landslides_in_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September,_2017.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Landslides_in_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September%2C_2017.png/220px-Landslides_in_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September%2C_2017.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Landslides_in_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September%2C_2017.png/330px-Landslides_in_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September%2C_2017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Landslides_in_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September%2C_2017.png/440px-Landslides_in_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico_caused_by_Hurricane_Maria_in_September%2C_2017.png 2x" data-file-width="1612" data-file-height="1188" /></a><figcaption>Landslides in Utuado, Puerto Rico caused by Hurricane Maria in September 2017. "Hurricane Maria triggered over 70,000 landslides across Puerto Rico." (Hughes and others, 2019)<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, triggered numerous landslides in Utuado. In many areas of Utuado there were more than 25 landslides per square mile due to the intense rainfall from Hurricane Maria.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:171017-F-FH950-0631_(37544301410).jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Relief efforts in Utuado"><img alt="Relief efforts in Utuado" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/171017-F-FH950-0631_%2837544301410%29.jpg/120px-171017-F-FH950-0631_%2837544301410%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="80" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/171017-F-FH950-0631_%2837544301410%29.jpg/180px-171017-F-FH950-0631_%2837544301410%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/171017-F-FH950-0631_%2837544301410%29.jpg/240px-171017-F-FH950-0631_%2837544301410%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1997" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Relief efforts in Utuado</div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span>  (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Utuado: <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Altos de Arena, \nSector El Guano in Arenas Abajo, \nSector Las Cuevas in Viv\xc3\xad Abajo, \nSector Mina de Oro in \xc3\x81ngeles Poblado, \nSector J\xc3\xa1canas in Caguana, \nMameyes, \nCaniaco, \nCayuco, \nChorreras, \nDon Alonso Motor, \nEl Ensanche, \nEl Hoyo in Mameyes, \nJudea, \nLa Granja, \nLa Playita, \nLoma Maestre, \nLomas Col\xc3\xb3n (Col\xc3\xb3n neighborhood),\nLos Pinos, \nMatadero Viejo, \nNuevo Londres, \nSector (Calle) San Antonio, \nSector Cuba, \nSector (Calle) Borinqu\xc3\xa9n, \nTetu\xc3\xa1n III</i></span>, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Calle Progreso in barrio-pueblo</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Embalse_Dos_Bocas_de_Utuado_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Lago Dos Bocas</i></span></figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">El Saltillo</i></span> waterfall</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dos_Bocas_Lake" title="Dos Bocas Lake">Dos Bocas Lake</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caonillas_Lake&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caonillas Lake (page does not exist)">Caonillas Lake</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Hacienda Roses</i></span></li>\n<li>Monuments to the Utuado Soldiers</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Caguana_Ceremonial_Ball_Courts_Site" title="Caguana Ceremonial Ball Courts Site">Caguana Ceremonial Ball Courts Site</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Abajo_State_Forest" title="R\xc3\xado Abajo State Forest">R\xc3\xado Abajo State Forest</a></li></ul>\n<p>With narrow streets leading up to a central plaza surrounded by a church and the governor\'s house, <b><a href="/wiki/Utuado_barrio-pueblo" title="Utuado barrio-pueblo">Utuado Pueblo</a></b> is an example of a town built during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_architecture" title="Spanish Colonial architecture">Spanish colonial</a> era of Puerto Rico. The <i>Iglesia San Miguel Arcangel</i>, the local Catholic parish, was founded in 1746. The current double-steepled church was built between 1872 and 1878 and is listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Caguana_Ceremonial_Ball_Courts_Site" title="Caguana Ceremonial Ball Courts Site">Caguana Ceremonial Park</a> and the Blanco Bridge or <i>Puente Blanco</i> located in <a href="/wiki/Arenas,_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arenas, Utuado, Puerto Rico">Arenas</a> barrio which connects Utuado with <a href="/wiki/Adjuntas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Adjuntas, Puerto Rico">Adjuntas</a>. Other buildings in Utuado Pueblo that retain their colonial architectural features include The Center for Art, Culture and Tourism in the old Tobacco Coop building, the old hospital <i>Hospital Catalina Figueras</i> and <i>Teatro San Miguel</i>, among others.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rio_Abajo_State_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Abajo State Forest">Rio Abajo State Forest</a> (<i>Bosque Estatal Rio Abajo</i>) is a 5,780-acre (23&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) forest reserve shared with Arecibo and home to 223 plants and wildlife species including: native ceiba (<i><a href="/wiki/Ceiba_pentandra" title="Ceiba pentandra">Ceiba pentandra</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Plantation_teak" title="Plantation teak">Asian teaks</a> (<i>Tectona</i> spp.), West Indian mahogany (<i><a href="/wiki/Swietenia_mahagoni" title="Swietenia mahagoni">Swietenia mahagoni</a></i>), Honduran mahogany (<i><a href="/wiki/Swietenia_humilis" title="Swietenia humilis">S. humilis</a></i>) and Australian pines (<i><a href="/wiki/Casuarina" title="Casuarina">Casuarina</a></i> spp.). It is also home to the federally endangered <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_broad-winged_hawk" title="Puerto Rican broad-winged hawk">Puerto Rican broad-winged hawk</a> (<i>Buteo platypterus brunnescens</i>) as well as a captive population of the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_parrot" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican parrot">Puerto Rican parrot</a> (<i>Amazona vittata</i>). Captive parrots are slowly being released into R\xc3\xado Abajo in an attempt to form a second population of parrots on the island.\n</p><p>East of the Rio Abajo Forest Reserve is the <a href="/wiki/Dos_Bocas_Lake" title="Dos Bocas Lake">Dos Bocas Lake</a> and dam, one of several man-made lakes in Utuado. From <i>El Embarcadero</i>, near routes 123 and 146, boats take guests around the water to one of the many restaurants for lakeside dining.\n</p><p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Caonillas_Lake&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caonillas Lake (page does not exist)">Caonillas Lake</a> and dam in the western region of Utuado is another man-made lake. This reservoir encompasses over 50 square miles (130&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and was constructed in 1948 by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Electric_Power_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority">Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg/220px-Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg/330px-Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg/440px-Utuado_Puerto_Rico_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1288" data-file-height="966" /></a><figcaption>View of Utuado Pueblo from Sabana Grande barrio</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Utuado has regained some of its coffee producing power and was the 3rd largest coffee producer in Puerto Rico in the 2002 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">USDA</a> Agricultural Census. It also produces oranges (ranked 4th), <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a> (ranked 6th) and <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a> (ranked 9th). It has been successful with livestock inventory ranking 3rd with hives of <a href="/wiki/Bees" class="mw-redirect" title="Bees">bees</a> and 13th with pigs. In terms of manufacturing, Utuado has facilities producing <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>, paper and stone.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Business">Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Utuado today is equipped with a modern and competitive telecommunications infrastructure. Major cell phone companies including <a href="/wiki/Claro_(mobile_phone_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="Claro (mobile phone network)">Claro</a> and <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mobility" title="AT&amp;T Mobility">AT&amp;T</a> offer <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile</a> coverage. Liberty Cablevision and <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a> offer <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable</a> and satellite television service, with Spanish and English channels as well as high-speed Internet service.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Like all municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Utuado is administered by a mayor. <a href="/wiki/Jorge_P%C3%A9rez_Heredia" title="Jorge P\xc3\xa9rez Heredia">Jorge "Jorgito" P\xc3\xa9rez Heredia</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="New Progressive Party of Puerto Rico">NPP</a>) took office as mayor of Utuado on January 16, 2021, succeeding <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Irizarry_Salv%C3%A1" title="Ernesto Irizarry Salv\xc3\xa1">Ernesto Irizarry Salv\xc3\xa1</a> (<a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">PDP</a>) after an 8-year term. Utuado belongs to Representative District 22, which is represented by one Representative. In 2020, Jorge Alfredo Rivera Segarra was elected as District Representative.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district V">Puerto Rico Senatorial district V</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Ruiz" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz">Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz</a> and Mart\xc3\xadn Vargas Morales (both <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">PDP</a>), were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nIn 2020, Marially Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (<a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">PDP</a>) succeeded Vargas Morales for her first term as District Senator, while Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz was elected to his second.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Baseball">Baseball</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Baseball"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Monta\xc3\xb1eses de Utuado</i></span> (<i>Utuado Mountaineers</i>) are a semi-professional baseball team based in Utuado that competes in the <a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_de_B%C3%A9isbol_Aficionado_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Federaci\xc3\xb3n de B\xc3\xa9isbol Aficionado de Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico Amateur Baseball Federation</a>\'s <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Liga Doble A</i></span>. The team achieved its first national championship in 1941 under the then <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Federaci\xc3\xb3n Deportiva del Norte</i></span> (<i>Sports Federation of the North</i>) as the Utuado Stars. Their second national championship was in 1970 under the current baseball federation. The team won their third national championship on September 1, 2007, against the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Bravos de <a href="/wiki/Cidra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cidra, Puerto Rico">Cidra</a></i></span> (<i>Cidra Braves</i>). On September 14, 2014, the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Monta\xc3\xb1eses</i></span> won their fourth national championship title against the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Brujos de <a href="/wiki/Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guayama, Puerto Rico">Guayama</a></i></span> (<i>Guayama Warlocks</i>) in a 7-game final.\n</p><p>On May 16, 2019, the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Monta\xc3\xb1eses</i></span> signed <a href="/wiki/Diamilette_Quiles" title="Diamilette Quiles">Diamilette Quiles</a>, making her not only the first female to play for the team, but also the first female signed in <span title="Spanish-language text"><span lang="es" style="font-style: normal;">B\xc3\xa9isbol Doble A</span></span>. Quiles was previously on the roster for the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Lobas de Arecibo</i></span> (<i>Arecibo Wolves</i>) in the Puerto Rico Women\'s Amateur Baseball Federation as well as playing <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_women%27s_national_softball_team" title="Puerto Rico women&#39;s national softball team">softball for Puerto Rico</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Table_tennis">Table tennis</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Table tennis"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Utuado\'s table tennis players include sisters <a href="/wiki/Adriana_D%C3%ADaz_(table_tennis)" title="Adriana D\xc3\xadaz (table tennis)">Adriana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melanie_D%C3%ADaz" title="Melanie D\xc3\xadaz">Melanie</a>, Gabriela and Fabiola D\xc3\xadaz, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Afanador" title="Brian Afanador">Brian Afanador</a> (cousin to the D\xc3\xadaz sisters), Daniel Gonz\xc3\xa1lez, Richard Pietri, <a href="/wiki/Daniely_R%C3%ADos" title="Daniely R\xc3\xados">Daniely R\xc3\xados</a> and Yomar Gonz\xc3\xa1lez, all members of the <i>\xc3\x81guilas de la Monta\xc3\xb1a</i> Table Tennis Club. Both Brian Afanador and Adriana Diaz, members of the International Table Tennis Federation World HOPES Team, have risen to prominence all over the Caribbean, Latin America and the world in their respective categories. The head coaches of the table tennis athletes are Bladimir Diaz, father of the D\xc3\xadaz sisters, and Eladio Afanador, a high-level performance program coach.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Utuado celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in September. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San Miguel Arcangel</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration to honor the archangel <a href="/wiki/Michael_(archangel)" title="Michael (archangel)">Michael</a> and generally features games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Utuado include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>National <a href="/wiki/Barbecue" title="Barbecue">BBQ</a> Festival \xe2\x80\x93 Originated by locals Samuel Kanig and Ramon G. Garcia, it is a one-day barbecue festival held on the first Sunday of January. It is an annual family event where people exhibit their own creativity by building unique barbecues made from common and uncommon household items. The festival has exhibited barbecue grills made from items such as a toolbox, coffin, light post and even an automobile.</li>\n<li>Juan Domingo Reyes Negr\xc3\xb3n Bike Day of Friendship \xe2\x80\x93 An annual bike day celebrated since 2001, between February and March. Celebrated in memory of Juan Domingo Reyes Negr\xc3\xb3n, a boy who died in a truck impact while on his bicycle in 2000, the idea was originated by the First Lady, Ivelisse Reyes and Director of the Municipal Office of Recreation and Sports at the time, Jos\xc3\xa9 F. Collazo, it has since been sponsored by the Municipal Government of Utuado and the Municipal Office of Recreation and Sports.</li>\n<li>Barrio <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngeles,_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="\xc3\x81ngeles, Utuado, Puerto Rico">\xc3\x81ngeles</a> Fiesta \xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li>Tierra Adentro Festival \xe2\x80\x93 Hosted annually by the Agricultural Technology department of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Utuado" title="University of Puerto Rico at Utuado">University of Puerto Rico at Utuado</a>, featuring arts and crafts by local artisans, cultural music, food and plant and animal exhibitions. This festival is held in April from a Wednesday to Sunday.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guarionex" title="Guarionex">Guarionex</a> Fiestas \xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngeles,_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="\xc3\x81ngeles, Utuado, Puerto Rico">\xc3\x81ngeles</a> Artisanal Fair \xe2\x80\x93 An annual arts &amp; crafts fair held in early May in \xc3\x81ngeles barrio featuring local artisans, music and food.</li>\n<li>Rosary Cross Day \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Longaniza" title="Longaniza">Longaniza</a> Festival \xe2\x80\x93 Celebrated its first year in June 2009, it was the lifelong dream of Don Jose A. Carmona "Don To\xc3\xb1o" to establish it to celebrate his legacy with his children (his own recipe for seasoning the sausage) and bring another special celebration to the mountain town and celebrate the longaniza.</li>\n<li>Otoao Cultural Festival \xe2\x80\x93 An annual cultural event held in the beginning of December celebrating Utuado\'s <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Taino</a> heritage.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>With the recent completion of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_10" title="Puerto Rico Highway 10">Highway 10</a>, Utuado has become one of the easiest towns in the interior mountainous region to reach from the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>. What used to be a 3-hour trip has been reduced to 1 hour and 30 minutes (to reach the central town). There are 64 bridges in Utuado.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many of Utuados roads and bridges were destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Utuado sustained approximately $36&#160;million in damages to its roads and bridges as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guzm\xc3\xa1_Vocero_2018_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guzm\xc3\xa1_Vocero_2018-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Funding to reconstruct a bridge in <a href="/wiki/Arenas,_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arenas, Utuado, Puerto Rico">Arenas</a> barrio, destroyed by Hurricane Maria in 2017, was made available in February 2021 and work was set to begin in June.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The flag, coat of arms and anthem of Utuado were all adopted in 1987, under the incumbency of Mayor <a href="/wiki/Waldemar_Quiles" title="Waldemar Quiles">Waldemar Quiles</a>. The flag and coat of arms were designed by Am\xc3\xadlcar Rivera D\xc3\xadaz; he is also the writer and composer of the anthem of Utuado.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:UtuadoFlag.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/UtuadoFlag.svg/150px-UtuadoFlag.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="100" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/UtuadoFlag.svg/225px-UtuadoFlag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/UtuadoFlag.svg/300px-UtuadoFlag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The flag consists of three colored stripes, green, brown and blue laid across; green for the mountains of the town, brown for the fertile soils and blue for the many rivers across the municipality. Centered in the flag is the sun of Otoao, a Ta\xc3\xadno representation of the sun.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Escudo_de_Utuado,_Puerto_Rico.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Escudo_de_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/150px-Escudo_de_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="252" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Escudo_de_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/225px-Escudo_de_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Escudo_de_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/300px-Escudo_de_Utuado%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="270" data-file-height="454" /></a><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The coat of arms bears a shield with a <a href="/wiki/Cem%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Cem\xc3\xad">cem\xc3\xad</a> (deity or ancestral spirit) and a silver sword. The color of the cem\xc3\xad alludes to the color of the earth, while the silver sword with a hilt in gold recalls <a href="/wiki/Michael_(archangel)" title="Michael (archangel)">Saint Michael</a>, the town\'s patron. The Ta\xc3\xadno mythological figure that appears on the upper left side symbolizes the "Caguana woman". The mine, the peak and the gold shovel crossed by the lamp of the copper miners establish the mineral wealth of this area. Finally, the blue background of the coat of arms remembers its skies, while the lower white stripe alludes to the <a href="/wiki/Viv%C3%AD_River" title="Viv\xc3\xad River">Viv\xc3\xad River</a> that crosses the town.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Anthem">Anthem</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Anthem"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The anthem of Utuado is titled "<i>Valle Bendito el de Mi Otoao</i>" (<i>Blessed Valley of my Otoao</i>).\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Utuado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are currently 20 schools under the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Education" title="Puerto Rico Department of Education">Puerto Rico Department of Education</a> system, 2 private schools and one college level institution; the vast majority of children in Utuado attend public schools. The main primary-level education institutions include Mar\xc3\xada Libertad G\xc3\xb3mez, Bernardo Gonz\xc3\xa1lez, and Judith A. Vivas, among others located outside Utuado Pueblo. Among the principal secondary-level institutions are the Francisco Ramos Middle School, Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera High School and Antonio Reyes Padilla Vocational High School. While most students attend the before-mentioned schools, Utuado also has two private education institutions, both primary-level: Colegio Utuade\xc3\xb1o San Jos\xc3\xa9 and Academia Dail\xc3\xa9n. Founded in 1979, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Utuado" title="University of Puerto Rico at Utuado">University of Puerto Rico at Utuado</a> is the youngest campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> and the only post secondary-level institution in Utuado, specializing in agricultural studies in areas such as pest control, horticulture, livestock industry and agricultural production.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people">Notable people</h2><span
